                10.1021/acsami.2c12894</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D14%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D47863-47871%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26issue%3D42%26author%3DR.%2BLuo%26author%3DJ.%2BZheng%26author%3DZ.%2BZhou%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.%2BHe%26title%3DStudy%2Bof%2BSynergistic%2BEffects%2Bof%2BCu%2Band%2BFe%2Bon%2BP2-Type%2BNa0.67MnO2%2Bfor%2BHigh%2BPerformance%2BNa-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.2c12894&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.chemmater.3c01196&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.2c12894&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Study of Synergistic Effects of Cu and Fe on P2-Type Na0.67MnO2 for High Performance Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Rui; Zheng, Junchao; Zhou, Zhiwei; Li, Jingyi; Li, Yunjiao; He, Zhenjiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">47863-47871</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-type Na0.67MnO2 with a stable structure and an open framework can provide numerous channels for fast Na+ de/intercalation, for which it is considered to be advantageous in application of the cathode material for Na-ion batteries.  However, the complex phase transition occurring during cycling and the lattice distortion triggered by the Jahn-Teller effect severely restrict its development.  Herein, the modified Na0.67MnO2 with Cu or Fe single-element doping as well as Cu and Fe double-element doping was synthesized by the sol-gel method, and the effects of doping on the crystal structure and electrochem. performances of Na0.67MnO2 were studied.  It was demonstrated that the phase of the material did not change after the introduction of Cu and Fe elements, and the cycling stability and rate performance were greatly improved by Cu and Fe double-doping owing to their synergistic effect.  The Na0.67Mn0.92Fe0.04Cu0.04O2 (NMFCO) cathode delivers discharge specific capacities of 110.5 mA h g-1 at 5 C and 91.8 mA h g-1 at 10 C and exhibits the high-capacity retention of 94.35% at 1 C and 90.68% at 5 C after 100 cycles.  Overall, this study offers a guiding direction for accelerating the modification of P2-type Na0.67MnO2 as a cathode active material for high performance Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref15" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201805381"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Since the discovery of high-transition-temp. (high-Tc) supercond. in layered copper oxides, many researchers have searched for similar behavior in other layered metal oxides involving 3d transition metals, such as cobalt and nickel.  Such attempts have so far failed, with the result that the copper oxide layer is thought to be essential for supercond.  Here, the authors report that NaxCoO2·yH2O (x ≈ 0.35, yr ≈ 1.3) is a superconductor with a Tc of about 5 K.  This compd. consists of two-dimensional CoO2 layers sepd. by a thick insulating layer of Na+ ions and H2O mols.  There is a marked resemblance in superconducting properties between the present material and high-Tc copper oxides, suggesting that the two systems have similar underlying physics.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref18" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1021/cm047737y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Takada, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Osada, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Izumi, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sakurai, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Takayama-Muromachi, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sasaki, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Characterization of Sodium Cobalt Oxides Related to P3-Phase Superconductor</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Characterization of Sodium Cobalt Oxides Related to P3-Phase Superconductor</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Takada, Kazunori; Osada, Minoru; Izumi, Fujio; Sakurai, Hiroya; Takayama-Muromachi, Eiji; Sasaki, Takayoshi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

                        cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Copper-Stabilized P'2-Type Layered Manganese Oxide Cathodes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ling, Yuexia; Zhou, Jiang; Guo, Shan; Fu, Hongwei; Zhou, Yifan; Fang, Guozhao; Wang, Liangbing; Lu, Bingan; Cao, Xinxin; Liang, Shuquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered sodium manganese oxides are promising low-cost and high-capacity cathode materials for commercialization of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  P'2-type Na0.67MnO2 with an orthorhombic structure has been considered as a significant candidate for SIBs.  However, the Jahn-Teller distortion and undesired phase transitions will lead to poor structural stability and unsatisfactory cycling performance.  Herein, a systematic investigation on partially copper-doped P'2-type Na0.67CuxMn1-xO2 (x = 0, 0.05, 0.1, and 0.2) series as cathodes for SIBs reveals the relationship between doping concns. and Na storage properties.  With proper copper content, P'2 Na0.67Cu0.1Mn0.9O2 exhibits a suppressed Jahn-Teller effect as well as relatively less phase transitions, which can deliver a high specific capacity of 222.7 mA h g-1 at 10 mA g-1 within 1.5-4.2 V, with a capacity retention of 76% at 1 A g-1 after 300 cycles.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Suppressing interlayer-gliding and Jahn-Teller effect in P2-type layered manganese oxide cathode via Mo doping for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Lin; Wang, Chenchen; Liu, Yanchen; Ren, Meng; Du, Juan; Chen, Aibing; Li, Fujun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Manganese-based layered oxides are one of the most promising cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to their high specific capacity and low cost of manganese and sodium.  However, they are limited by the poor cycling stability caused by irreversible phase transitions and Jahn-Teller effect of Mn3+.  Herein, Mo-doped P2-Na0.67Mn1-xMoxO2 suppress the irreversible phase transition of P2-OP4 resulted from gliding of MnO2-slabs.  It reveals that no phase transition occurs under high voltage via Mo elements doping into MnO6-layers.  P2-Na0.67Mn1-xMoxO2 displays high cyclic stability with a high capacity retention of 86.4% after 100 cycles and improved rate performance with an av. working voltage of 2.61 V.  The research provides a new perspective for designing novel layered oxide cathodes design toward high-performance SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref24" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1021/acsmaterialslett.9b00347"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rahman, M.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An Ordered P2/P3 Composite Layered Oxide Cathode with Long Cycle Life in Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Rahman, Muhammad Mominur; Mao, Jing; Kan, Wang Hay; Sun, Cheng-Jun; Li, Luxi; Zhang, Yan; Avdeev, Maxim; Du, Xi-Wen; Lin, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Materials Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing stable cathode materials represents a crucial step toward long-life Na-ion batteries.  P2-type layered oxides are important as cathodes for their reversibility, but their long-term performance in full cells remains a key challenge.  Here, we report Na0.75Co0.125Cu0.125Fe0.125Ni0.125Mn0.5O2 with an intergrowth of ordered P2 and P3 phases, studied by neutron diffraction and Rietveld refinement.  A stable electrochem. performance is achieved in Na half cells with 100% capacity retention at a rate of C/10 after 100 cycles (initial capacity of 90 mAh/g), 96% capacity retention at a rate of 1 C after 500 cycles (initial capacity of 70 mAh/g), and 85% capacity retention at a rate of 5 C after 1000 cycles (initial capacity of 55 mAh/g).  Stable full cell performance is achieved with 84.2% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at a rate of 1 C.  Synchrotron x-ray diffraction, spectroscopy, and imaging are applied to elucidate the relationship between chem./structural evolution and battery performance.  A reversible local and global structural evolution is obsd. during initial cycles.  The challenges with enabling prolonged cycling (beyond 1000 cycles) may be assocd. with Fe dissoln. and formation of a Cu oxide phase.  This study implies that cathodes with complex chem. and structural formations may stabilize electrochem. performance and highlights the importance of decoupling the contribution of each transition metal to performance degrdn.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref25" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1021/cm000721x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahn, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The intercalation of H2O into P2-Na2/3[CoxNi1/3-xMn2/3]O2 (x = 0, 1/6, 1/3) and T2 or O2 structure Li2/3[CoxNi1/3-xMn2/3]O2 (x = 0, 1/6, 1/3) was studied by x-ray diffraction and TGA.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Air-stability is one of the most important considerations for the practical application of electrode materials in energy-harvesting/storage devices, ranging from solar cells to rechargeable batteries.  The promising P2-layered sodium transition metal oxides (P2-NaxTmO2) often suffer from structural/chem. transformations when contacted with moist air.  However, these elaborate transitions and the evaluation rules towards air-stable P2-NaxTmO2 have not yet been clearly elucidated.  Herein, taking P2-Na0.67MnO2 and P2-Na0.67Ni0.33Mn0.67O2 as key examples, we unveil the comprehensive structural/chem. degrdn. mechanisms of P2-NaxTmO2 in different ambient atmospheres by using various microscopic/spectroscopic characterizations and first-principle calcns.  The extent of bulk structural/chem. transformation of P2-NaxTmO2 is detd. by the amt. of extd. Na+, which is mainly compensated by Na+/H+ exchange.  By expanding our study to a series of Mn-based oxides, we reveal that the air-stability of P2-NaxTmO2 is highly related to their oxidn. features in the first charge process and further propose a practical evaluating rule assocd. with redox couples for air-stable NaxTmO2 cathodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref27" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA02067A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Konarov, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, J.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been intensively investigated as a potential alternative to lithium-ion batteries.  Among the studied cathodes, the cost-effective P2-type Na2/3MnO2 cathode is particularly attractive because it can deliver high capacity and high energy d.  However, its cyclability during prolonged use remains an issue because of the Jahn-Teller distortion assocd. with the presence of Mn3+.  In this study, the effect of Ni doping on the electrochem. properties of Na2/3MnO2 was investigated by varying the Ni content in the range of x = 0-0.2 in Na2/3[Mn1-xNix]O2.  Of these materials, Na2/3[Mn0.8Ni0.2]O2 exhibited the best electrochem. performance in terms of capacity and retention as well as improved thermal properties.  Although in situ operando synchrotron X-ray diffraction anal. of the structural stability indicated that Na2/3[Mn0.8Ni0.2]O2 underwent a bi-phasic reaction (a P2-O2 transformation when charged to 4.3 V), the resulting vol. change from P2 to O2 was only approx. 10%.  This low vol. change was possible because of the Ni2+ substitution of partial Mn3+ in the crystal structure, which is thought to have suppressed the cooperative Jahn-Teller distortion, as demonstrated by extended X-ray absorption fine structure anal.  As a result, the post-cycled Na2/3[Mn0.8Ni0.2]O2 was able to maintain its original structure, whereas structural disintegration was obsd. for Na2/3MnO2.  Our findings provide a potential new path to utilize cost-effective Mn-rich high-capacity cathode materials for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref28" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/0921-4526(93)90108-I"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rodríguez-Carvajal, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Advances in Magnetic Structure Determination by Neutron Powder Diffraction</span>. <i>Phys.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reducing carbon in LiFePO4/C composite electrodes to maximize specific energy, volumetric energy, and tap density</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Zhaohui; Dahn, J. R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Efforts were made to synthesize LiFePO4/C composites showing good rate capability and high energy d. while attempting to minimize the amt. of carbon in the composite.  First, three carbon-coated samples, one coated with carbon after the synthesis of pure LiFePO4, one synthesized with sugar added before the heating steps, and one synthesized with sugar added before heating and subsequently coated with carbon, were studied.  The resulting carbon contents for these samples are 2.7, 3.5, and 6.2 wt %, resp.  The latter two samples had comparable rate capabilities to the LiFePO4/C composite (15 wt % carbon).  The synthesis of LiFePO4 with sugar added before heating is the best method because it gives particles having uniform small size that are covered by carbon.  Further studies of samples made by this method show that a very small percentage of carbon, even less than 1 wt %, causes a significant increase in rate capability, but unfortunately, a dramatic decrease in tap d.  To make LiFePO4/C composites having good rate capability, high energy d., and high tap d., the carbon content and method for coating carbon onto the LiFePO4 particles must be given careful attention.  However, based on the studies reported here, we are not certain that all desired parameters can be simultaneously achieved, and this may limit the usefulness of LiFePO4 in some practical applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref32" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1021/acs.accounts.7b00031"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical Techniques for Intercalation Electrode Materials in Rechargeable Batteries</span>. <i>Acc.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical Techniques for Intercalation Electrode Materials in Rechargeable Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yujie; Gao, Tao; Fan, Xiulin; Han, Fudong; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">50</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1022-1031</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACHRE4</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0001-4842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Understanding of the thermodn. and kinetic properties of electrode materials is of great importance to develop new materials for high performance rechargeable batteries.  Compared with computational understanding of phys. and chem. properties of electrode materials, exptl. methods provide direct and convenient evaluation of these properties.  Often, the information gained from exptl. work can not only offer feedback for the computational methods but also provide useful insights for improving the performance of materials.  However, accurate exptl. quantification of some properties can still be challenging.  Among them, chem. diffusion coeff. is one representative example.  It is one of the most crucial parameters detg. the kinetics of intercalation compds., which are by far the dominant electrode type used in rechargeable batteries.  Therefore, it is of significance to quant. evaluate this parameter.  For this purpose, various electrochem. techniques have been invented, for example, galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT), potentiostatic intermittent titrn. technique (PITT), electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS), and cyclic voltammetry (CV).  One salient advantage of these electrochem. techniques over other characterization techniques is that some implicit thermodn. and kinetic quantities can be linked with the readily measurable elec. signals, current, and voltage, with very high precision.  Nevertheless, proper application of these techniques requires not just an understanding of the structure and chem. of the studied materials but sufficient knowledge of the phys. model for ion transport within solid host materials and the anal. method to solve for chem. diffusion coeff.Our group has been focusing on using various electrochem. techniques to investigate battery materials, as well as developing models for studying some emerging materials.  In this Account, the principles of the aforementioned four electrochem. techniques and the corresponding anal. equations for calcg. the chem. diffusion coeffs. are first briefly summarized, followed by a discussion of the hidden assumptions for deriving these anal. equations and the resulting limitations in their implementation.  To address these limitations, various corrections have been made in the literature.  Nevertheless, the phase transition behavior, which is the typical feature for many intercalation materials, is barely considered.  Here we retrospect our previous work on developing a two-phase model for describing the phase transition behavior of some intercalation compds. and discuss how to obtain the chem. diffusion coeffs. based on the model, using LiFePO4 as an example material.  After that, we have a discussion on the methodol. for using electrochem. techniques to investigate new material features.  It is our hope that this Account can serve as a call for more endeavors into the development of novel electrochem. tools for battery research.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref33" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1149/1.2128939"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">John

                        cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Band theory and Mott insulators:  Hubbard U instead of Stoner I</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Anisimov, V. I.; Zaanen, Jan; Andersen, Ole K.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review B:  Condensed Matter and Materials Physics</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors propose a form for the exchange-correlation potential in local-d. band theory, appropriate to Mott insulators.  The idea is to use the "constrained-local-d.-approxn." Hubbard parameter U as the quantity relating the single-particle potentials-to the magnetic- (and orbital-) order parameters.  The authors' energy functional is that of the local-d. approxn. plus the mean-field approxn. to the remaining part of the U term.  They argue that such a method should make sense, if one accepts the Hubbard model and the success of constrained-local-d.-approxn. parameter calcns.  By using this ab initio scheme, they find that all late-3d-transition-metal monoxides, as well as the parent compds. of the high-Tc compds., are large-gap magnetic insulators of the charge-transfer type.  Further, the method predicts that LiNiO2 is a low-spin ferromagnet and NiS a local-moment p-type metal.  The present version of the scheme fails for the early-3d-transition-metal monoxides and for the late 3d transition metals.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref37" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1021/acs.jpca.0c01375"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kresse, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Furthmu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Efficient Iterative Schemes for Ab Initio Total-Energy Calculations Using a Plane-Wave Basis Set</span>. <i>Phys.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficient iterative schemes for ab initio total-energy calculations using a plane-wave basis set</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kresse, G.; Furthmueller, J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review B: Condensed Matter</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors present an efficient scheme for calcg. the Kohn-Sham ground state of metallic systems using pseudopotentials and a plane-wave basis set.  In the first part the application of Pulay's DIIS method (direct inversion in the iterative subspace) to the iterative diagonalization of large matrixes will be discussed.  This approach is stable, reliable, and minimizes the no. of order Natoms3 operations.  In the second part, we will discuss an efficient mixing scheme also based on Pulay's scheme.  A special "metric" and a special "preconditioning" optimized for a plane-wave basis set will be introduced.  Scaling of the method will be discussed in detail for non-self-consistent and self-consistent calcns.  It will be shown that the no. of iterations required to obtain a specific precision is almost independent of the system size.  Altogether an order Natoms2 scaling is found for systems contg. up to 1000 electrons.  If we take into account that the no. of k points can be decreased linearly with the system size, the overall scaling can approach Natoms.  They have implemented these algorithms within a powerful package called VASP (Vienna ab initio simulation package).  The program and the techniques have been used successfully for a large no. of different systems (liq. and amorphous semiconductors, liq. simple and transition metals, metallic and semiconducting surfaces, phonons in simple metals, transition metals, and semiconductors) and turned out to be very reliable.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref38" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.50.17953"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Blöchl, P.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical porous nitrogen, oxygen, and phosphorus ternary doped hollow biomass carbon spheres for high-speed and long-life potassium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Mengmeng; Kong, Qingquan; Feng, Wei; Yao, Weitang; Wang, Qingyuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">45-59</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Limited lithium resources have promoted the exploration of new battery technologies.  Among them, potassium-ion batteries are considered as promising alternatives.  At present, com. graphite and other carbon-based materials have shown good prospects as anodes for potassium-ion batteries.  However, the vol. expansion and structural collapse caused by periodic K+ insertion/extn. have severely restricted further development and application of potassium-ion batteries.  A hollow biomass carbon ball (NOP-PB) ternarily doped with N, O, and P was synthesized and used as the neg. electrode of a potassium-ion battery.  XPS, Fourier-transform IR spectroscopy, and transmission electron microscopy confirmed that the hollow biomass carbon spheres were successfully doped with N, O, and P.  Further anal. proved that N, O, and P ternary doping expands the interlayer distance of the graphite surface and introduces more defect sites.  DFT calcns. simultaneously proved that the K adsorption energy of the doped structure is greatly improved.  The solid hollow hierarchical porous structure buffers the vol. expansion of the potassium insertion process, maintains the original structure after a long cycle and promotes the transfer of potassium ions and electrons.  Therefore, the NOP-PB neg. electrode shows extremely enhanced electrochem. performance, including high specific capacity, excellent long-term stability, and good rate stability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tolba, S. Chem. Phys.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2010</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>132</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">15</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">154104</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1063/1.3382344</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D132%26publication_year%3D2010%26pages%3D154104%26journal%3DJ.%2BChem.%2BPhys.%26issue%3D15%26author%3DS.%2BGrimme%26author%3DJ.%2BAntony%26author%3DS.%2BEhrlich%26author%3DH.%2BKrieg%26title%3DA%2BConsistent%2Band%2BAccurate%2BAb%2BInitio%2BParametrization%2Bof%2BDensity%2BFunctional%2BDispersion%2BCorrection%2B%2528DFT-D%2529%2Bfor%2Bthe%2B94%2BElements%2BH-Pu%26doi%3D10.1063%252F1.3382344&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.chemmater.3c01196&amp;doiOfLink=10.1063%2F1.3382344&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A consistent and accurate ab initio parametrization of density functional dispersion correction (DFT-D) for the 94 elements H-Pu</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Grimme, Stefan; Antony, Jens; Ehrlich, Stephan; Krieg, Helge</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">132</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">154104/1-154104/19</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCPSA6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-9606</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Institute of Physics</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The method of dispersion correction as an add-on to std. Kohn-Sham d. functional theory (DFT-D) has been refined regarding higher accuracy, broader range of applicability, and less empiricism.  The main new ingredients are atom-pairwise specific dispersion coeffs. and cutoff radii that are both computed from first principles.  The coeffs. for new eighth-order dispersion terms are computed using established recursion relations.  System (geometry) dependent information is used for the first time in a DFT-D type approach by employing the new concept of fractional coordination nos. (CN).  They are used to interpolate between dispersion coeffs. of atoms in different chem. environments.  The method only requires adjustment of two global parameters for each d. functional, is asymptotically exact for a gas of weakly interacting neutral atoms, and easily allows the computation of at. forces.  Three-body nonadditivity terms are considered.  The method has been assessed on std. benchmark sets for inter- and intramol. noncovalent interactions with a particular emphasis on a consistent description of light and heavy element systems.  The mean abs. deviations for the S22 benchmark set of noncovalent interactions for 11 std. d. functionals decrease by 15%-40% compared to the previous (already accurate) DFT-D version.  Spectacular improvements are found for a tripeptide-folding model and all tested metallic systems.  The rectification of the long-range behavior and the use of more accurate C6 coeffs. also lead to a much better description of large (infinite) systems as shown for graphene sheets and the adsorption of benzene on an Ag(111) surface.  For graphene it is found that the inclusion of three-body terms substantially (by about 10%) weakens the interlayer binding.  We propose the revised DFT-D method as a general tool for the computation of the dispersion energy in mols. and solids of any kind with DFT and related (low-cost) electronic structure methods for large systems.  (c) 2010 American Institute of Physics.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref43" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1002/jcc"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barone, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Casarin, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Forrer, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pavone, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sambi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vittadini, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Role and Effective Treatment of Dispersive Forces in Materials: Polyethylene and Graphite Crystals as Test Cases</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tuning P2-Structured Cathode Material by Na-Site Mg Substitution for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qin-Chao; Meng, Jing-Ke; Yue, Xin-Yang; Qiu, Qi-Qi; Song, Yun; Wu, Xiao-Jing; Fu, Zheng-Wen; Xia, Yong-Yao; Shadike, Zulipiya; Wu, Jinpeng; Yang, Xiao-Qing; Zhou, Yong-Ning</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">141</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Most P2-type layered oxides suffer from multiple voltage plateaus, due to Na+/vacancy-order superstructures caused by strong interplay between Na-Na electrostatic interactions and charge ordering in the transition metal layers.  Here, Mg ions are successfully introduced into Na sites in addn. to the conventional transition metal sites in P2-type Na0.7[Mn0.6Ni0.4]O2 as new cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  Mg ions in the Na layer serve as "pillars" to stabilize the layered structure, esp. for high-voltage charging, meanwhile Mg ions in the transition metal layer can destroy charge ordering.  More importantly, Mg ion occupation in both sodium and transition metal layers will be able to create "Na-O-Mg" and "Mg-O-Mg" configurations in layered structures, resulting in ionic O 2p character, which allocates these O 2p states on top of those interacting with transition metals in the O-valence band, thus promoting reversible oxygen redox.  This innovative design contributes smooth voltage profiles and high structural stability.  Na0.7Mg0.05[Mn0.6Ni0.2Mg0.15]O2 exhibits superior electrochem. performance, esp. good capacity retention at high current rate under a high cutoff voltage (4.2 V).  A new P2 phase is formed after charge, rather than an O2 phase for the unsubstituted material.  Besides, multiple intermediate phases are obsd. during high-rate charging.  Na-ion transport kinetics are mainly affected by elemental-related redox couples and structural reorganization.  These findings will open new opportunities for designing and optimizing layer-structured cathodes for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref46" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.commatsci.2014.09.021"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zunger, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, S.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ferreira, L.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Although the formalism that allows the calcn. of alloy thermodn. properties from first-principles has been known for decades, its practical implementation has so far remained a tedious process.  The Alloy Theoretic Automated Toolkit (ATAT) drastically simplifies this procedure by implementing decision rules based on formal statistical anal. that frees the researchers from a const. monitoring during the calcn. process and automatically "glues" together the input and the output of various codes, in order to provide a high-level interface to the calcn. of alloy thermodn. properties from first-principles.  ATAT implements the Structure Inversion Method (SIM), also known as the Connolly-Williams method, in combination with semi-grand-canonical Monte Carlo simulations.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Software tools for high-throughput CALPHAD from first-principles data</span></div><div class="casAuthors">van de Walle, Axel; Sun, Ruoshi; Hong, Qi-Jun; Kadkhodaei, Sara</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">CALPHAD: Computer Coupling of Phase Diagrams and Thermochemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">58</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">70-81</span>CODEN:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0364-5916</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We present a set of software tools that largely automate the process of converting ab initio data into thermodn. databases that can readily be imported into std. thermodn. modeling softwares.  These tools are based on the Special Quasirandom Structures (SQS) formalism, extended to transparently handle, not only traditional fcc, bcc and hcp solid solns., but also multiple-sublattice structures with possible sublattice disorder.  A large database of pre-generated SQS is provided that covers over 30 of the most common multi-sublattice structures and spans the compn. ranges of each of their sublattices.  In addn., we exploit a theor. justified and robust method to address the issue of assigning free energies to mech. unstable "virtual" phases, thus providing a compelling soln. to a long-standing problem in CALPHAD modeling, esp. in the context of ab initio data.  We also propose a simple low-order approxn. scheme to include short-range order effects that requires no addnl. ab initio input.  The resulting thermodyamic database seamlessly combines ab initio data (formation energies and, optionally, vibrational free energies) with elemental Scientific Group Thermodata Europe (SGTE) data.  The proposed tools provide a clear path to expand the coverage of high-throughput efforts towards non-stoichiometric phases and non-zero temps.  The generated free energy models can also provide very good starting points to perform complex thermodn. assessments, esp. in cases where the available exptl. data poorly constrain some thermodn. parameters. However, these elaborate transitions and the evaluation rules towards air-stable P2-NaxTmO2 have not yet been clearly elucidated.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The controlled synthesis of birnessite nanoflowers via H2O2 reducing KMnO4 for efficient adsorption and photooxidation activity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yang; Jiang, Guanjie; Ouyang, Nanqi; Qin, Zhangjie; Lan, Shuai; Zhang, Qin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Frontiers in Chemistry (Lausanne, Switzerland)</span>

The method relies on the molar ratios of KMnO4 and H2O2 redox reacting species to drive the prodn. of birnessite nanoflowers under acidic conditions.  The molar ratios of KMnO4 and H2O2 are the key to the crystal structure of the as-prepd.  It was found that when the molar ratios of KMnO4 and H2O2 is from 1:1.25 to 1:1.90, the sample is birnessite nanoflowers, and when the ratio is increased to 1:2.0, the sample is a mixt. of birnessite nanoflowers and feitknechtite nanoplates.  Among the as-prepd. samples, BF-1.85 (molar ratios of KMnO4 and H2O2 is 1:1.85) shows the highest capacity for Pb2+ adsorption (2,955 mmol/kg) and greatest degrdn. efficiency of phenol and TOC.                 10.1021/acs.inorgchem.6b01465</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D55%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D10248-10258%26journal%3DInorg.%2BChem.%26issue%3D20%26author%3DQ.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BLiao%26author%3DW.%2BXu%26author%3DY.%2BRen%26author%3DK.%2BJ.%2BLivi%26author%3DM.%2BZhu%26title%3DSynthesis%2Bof%2BBirnessite%2Bin%2Bthe%2BPresence%2Bof%2BPhosphate%252C%2BSilicate%252C%2Bor%2BSulfate%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.inorgchem.6b01465&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.chemmater.3c01196&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.6b01465&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of Birnessite in the Presence of Phosphate, Silicate, or Sulfate</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qian; Liao, Xianya; Xu, Wenqian; Ren, Yang; Livi, Kenneth J.; Zhu, Mengqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Inorganic Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">55</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10248-10258</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">INOCAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0020-1669</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered manganese (Mn) oxides, such as birnessite, are versatile materials in industrial applications and common minerals mediating elemental cycling in natural environment.  Many of birnessite properties are controlled by Mn(III) concn. and particle sizes.  Thus, it is important to synthesize birnessite nanoparticles with controlled Mn(III) concns. and sizes so that one can tune its properties for many applications.  Birnessite was synthesized in the presence of oxyanions (phosphate, silicate, or sulfate) during reductive pptn. of KMnO4 by HCl and characterized using multiple synchrotron X-ray techniques, electron microscopy, and diffuse reflectance UV-vis spectroscopy.  Results indicate that all three anions decrease MnO6 sheet sizes, attributed to oxyanion adsorption on edges of the sheets, inhibiting their lateral growth.  As a result of decreased sizes, sheets undergo significant structural contraction.  Meanwhile, Mn(III) concn. significantly increases with increasing oxyanion/Mn ratio.  The increased Mn(III) concn., along with the decreased size, enlarges both direct and indirect band gaps of birnessite.  Phosphate imposes the strongest influence, followed by silicate and then by sulfate, consistent with their decreasing adsorption affinity.  Reacting with 1 M KOH soln. effectively removed the adsorbed oxyanions while leading to increased sheet sizes, probably due to oriented attachment-driven particle growth mechanisms.  The results have important implications for developing highly performed birnessite materials, for example, small size Mn(III)-rich birnessite for photochem. and catalytic applications, as well as for understanding chem. compositional variations of naturally occurring birnessite.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref57" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1039/C8EE02991A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Somerville, J.                         cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nature of the "Z"-phase in layered Na-ion battery cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Somerville, James W.; Sobkowiak, Adam; Tapia-Ruiz, Nuria; Billaud, Juliette; Lozano, Juan G.; House, Robert A.; Gallington, Leighanne C.; Ericsson, Tore; Haggstrom, Lennart; Roberts, Matthew R.; Maitra, Urmimala; Bruce, Peter G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2223-2232</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered sodium transition metal oxides with the P2 structure, e.g.  Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2, are regarded as candidates for Na-ion battery cathodes.  On charging, extn. of Na destabilizes the P2 phase (ABBA oxide ion stacking) in which Na+ is in trigonal prismatic coordination, resulting in layer gliding and formation of an O2 phase (ABAC stacking) with octahedral coordination.  However, many related compds. do not exhibit such a simple P2 to O2 transition but rather form a so called "Z"-phase.  Substituting Ni by Fe in Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 is attractive as it reduces cost.  The Fe contg. compds., such as Na2/3[Ni1/6Mn1/2Fe1/3]O2, form a "Z"-phase when charged above 4.1 V vs.  Na+/Na.  By combining ex situ and operando X-ray diffraction with scanning transmission electron microscopy and simulated diffraction patterns, we demonstrate that the "Z"-phase is most accurately described as a continuously changing intergrowth structure which evolves from P2 to O2 through the OP4 structure as an intermediate.  On charging, Na+ removal results in O-type stacking faults within the P2 structure which increase in proportion.  At 50% O-type stacking faults, the ordered OP4 phase forms and on further charging more O-type stacking faults are formed progressing towards a pure O2 structure.  This gives the superficial appearance of a solid soln.  Furthermore, in contrast to some previous studies, we did not detect Fe migration at any state-of-charge using 57Fe-Mossbauer spectroscopy.  It was, however, found that the Fe-substitution serves to disrupt cation ordering in the material.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref58" class="refNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit58" data-doi="10.1039/B602491B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Casas-Cabanas, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rodríguez-Carvajal, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Canales-Vázquez, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Palacín, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Two sets of lab.-prepd. and industrial Ni hydroxide samples were studied and their microstructure characterized by Rietveld refinement, using a spherical harmonic-implemented algorithm with both n and x-ray powder diffraction data.  The anisotropic line broadening present in their patterns is related to the anisotropy in size, as β-Ni(OH)2 exhibits a platelet shape.  The detd. crystallite sizes are consistent with mean particle diams. measured by TEM.  The relative degree of stacking faults was estd. from the extent of shifts in reflections 10l where l ≠ 0 and it is larger for samples with smaller particle/crystallite sizes.  This approach, involving independent assessment of the crystallite size and the relative amt. of stacking faults, confirms that samples with small crystallite size are those with more stacking faults.  The results of the electrochem. tests on both sets of samples indicate that the particle/crystallite size is the primary factor detg. the electrochem. yield and that the gradual appearance of stacking faults with decreasing size creates a synergic effect in the increase of capacity.  Thus, there exists a threshold size of ∼350 Å in diam. and 100 Å in thickness below which the degree of faulting is correlated to the electrochem. capacity values achieved.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref59" class="refNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit59" data-doi="10.1039/a701037k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Delmas, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tessier, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Stacking Faults in the Structure of Nickel Hydroxide: A Rationale of Its High Electrochemical Activity</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The most common MXene compn. Ti3C2Tx (T = F, O) shows outstanding stability as anode for sodium ion batteries (100% of capacity retention after 530 cycles with charge efficiency &gt;99.7%).  However, the reversibility of the intercalation/deintercalation process is strongly affected by the synthesis parameters detg., in turn, significant differences in the material structure.  This study proposes a new approach to identify the crystal features influencing the performances, using a structural model built with a multitechnique approach that allows exploring the short-range order of the lamella.  The model is then used to det. the long-range order by inserting defective elements into the structure.  With this strategy it is possible to fit the MXene diffraction patterns, obtain the structural parameters including the stoichiometric compn. of the terminations (neutron data), and quantify the structural disorder which can be used to discriminate the phases with the best electrochem. properties.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref64"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref64" class="refNumLink">64</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit64" data-doi="10.1016/S0167-2738(03)00035-3"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Julien, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Massot, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Baddour-Hadjean, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Franger, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bach, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pereira-Ramos, J. This local probe is capable of analyzing directly the near-neighbor environment of O coordination around Mn and Li cations.  Four types of sol-gel birnessite (SGB) are considered: Li birnessite (Li-Bir), Na birnessite (Na-Bir), sol-gel birnessite (SG-Bir), and sol-gel Co-doped birnessite (SGCo-Bir).                         cas_cit66R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">66</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">XRD/Raman spectroscopy studies of the mechanism of (de)intercalation of Na+ from/into highly crystalline birnessite</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Scheitenberger, Philipp; Brimaud, Sylvain; Linden, Mika</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Advances</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to its low-cost and environmental friendliness, birnessite-type manganese oxide has attracted wide interest for use as a cathode material in electrochem. energy storage applications.  The mechanisms of energy storage and release have been studied in some detail during the last decade, but despite some agreement, some aspects of the storage and release mechanisms are still under debate.  The main reason for this, we argue, is the varying interpretations of Raman spectroscopy data in the literature.  Therefore, we undertook a detailed correlative Raman spectroscopy/XRD study in combination with cyclic voltammetry.  Raman spectroscopy allowed for straightforward differentiation between symmetry changes during the (de)intercalation of Na-ions.  More specifically, through the use of highly cryst. birnessite samples it is suggested that Raman spectra are sensitive to the lattice parameters β and d001, which allowed us to derive unprecedented details of the changes in the birnessite structure that occur upon Na+ (de)intercalation.  Furthermore, it is shown that the reversible hexagonal/monoclinic symmetry transition during the course of a charge/discharge cycle is a prerequisite for effective charge storage.  Based on the results, a detailed mechanism describing the (de)intercalation of Na+ from/into birnessite is presented.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref67"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref67" class="refNumLink">67</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit67" data-doi="10.1016/j.ceramint.2022.11.002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Venkatesh, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Priyanga, G. This is concomitant with Fe and Co doping showing improved cyclic stability when cycled under similar conditions.                         cas_cit69R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">69</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na2/3Li1/9[Ni2/9Li1/9Mn2/3]O2: A High-Performance Solid-Solution Reaction Layered Oxide Cathode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zheng-Yao; Ma, Xiaobai; Sun, Kai; He, Linfeng; Li, Yuqing; Chen, Dongfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>

The Li0.97Na0.03Ni0.5Co0.2Mn0.3O2 material has a high tap d. of 2.17 g cm-3 that meets the com. requirement in Li ion batteries (LIBs).                         cas_cit74R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">74</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unveiling Oxygen Redox Activity in P2-Type NaxNi0.25Mn0.68O2 High-Energy Cathode for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Massaro, Arianna; Munoz-Garcia, Ana B.; Prosini, Pier Paolo; Gerbaldi, Claudio; Pavone, Michele</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2470-2480</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries are emerging as convenient energy-storage devices for large-scale applications.  Enhanced energy d. and cycling stability are key in the optimization of functional cathode materials such as P2-type layered transition metal oxides.  High operating voltage can be achieved by enabling anionic reactions, but irreversibility of O2-/O2n-/O2 evolution still limits this chance, leading to extra capacity at first cycle that is not fully recovered.  Here, we dissect this intriguing oxygen redox activity in Mn-deficient NaxNi0.25Mn0.68O2 from first-principles, by analyzing the formation of oxygen vacancies and dioxygen complexes at different stages of sodiation.  We identify low-energy intermediates that release mol. O2 at high voltage, and we show how to improve the overall cathode stability by partial substitution of Ni with Fe.                         cas_cit75R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">75</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ru-Doping of P2-NaxMn0.75Ni0.25O2-Layered Oxides for High-Energy Na-Ion Battery Cathodes: First-Principles Insights on Activation and Control of Reversible Oxide Redox Chemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Massaro, Arianna; Langella, Aniello; Gerbaldi, Claudio; Elia, Giuseppe Antonio; Munoz-Garcia, Ana B.; Pavone, Michele</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Design and development of high-energy, efficient, and structurally stable pos. electrodes for Na-ion batteries (NIBs) have recently been focusing on layered transition metal oxides (NaxTMO2, 0 &lt; x &lt; 1).  When doped with late transition metals, the redox reactions ensuring the charge compensation upon Na+ removal can rely on the direct participation of anionic chem., with encouraging outcomes in terms of both energy d. and power.  However, the control of reversible O2-/O- reactions is still a major issue, as the undesired release of O2 can lead to detrimental effects on cathode capacity and overall cell stability.  The fine-tuning of metal-oxygen bond covalency has recently emerged as a promising strategy toward the reversible access of oxygen redox.  Following the route paved by Ru-based Li-rich cathode materials, we hereby present a first-principles investigation of a Ru-doped NaxTMO2 (TM = Ru, Ni, and Mn) system and the related structural and electronic properties of interest for NIB applications.  We aim to dissect the specific role of each element sublattice in compensating the electronic charge along desodiation, with a major focus on the anionic contribution.  The oxygen activity is addressed in the high-voltage range (i.e.,xNa = 0.25), and the underlying mechanism is derived from PBE + U(-D3BJ) calcns.  We also discuss the effects of Mn deficiency as a suitable site for the formation of low-energy superoxide species via preferential breaking of the Ni-O bond.  Conversely, breaking a Ru-O bond is unlikely to occur, which assesses the key role of the Ru dopant in stabilizing the oxide lattice and enabling the desired reversible conditions.  Our results also highlight the oxygen vacancy formation energy as an effective descriptor for different activities toward the O2-/O-/O2 evolution.  All these theor. insights can be useful to drive further exptl. efforts toward the optimal design of efficient and high-energy NIB cathodes with enhanced practical reversible capacity.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref76"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref76" class="refNumLink">76</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit76" data-doi="10.1111/jace.18494"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Massaro, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Langella, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Muñoz-García, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In the search for high-energy cathode materials for Na-ion batteries (NIBs), Fe-doped layered transition metal oxides have been recently proposed as promising systems that can ensure improved reversible capacity at high working voltage.  Exploiting the anionic redox chem. in this class of materials represents a great advance for the energy storage community, but uncontrolled oxidn. process can lead to the formation of unbound mol. oxygen, with detrimental effects on overall capacity and stability upon cycling.  The higher TM-O covalency provided by Fe doping seems to prevent oxygen loss and ensure full capacity recovery.  Understanding anionic processes and the underlying mechanism with atomistic details can reinforce the exptl. efforts and help to outline rational design strategies for novel high-performing NIB cathodes.  To this end, we present a state-of-the-art first-principles study on the P2-type NaxTMO2 (TM = Fe, Ni, and Mn-NFNMO) oxide.  We compare structural and electronic features of stoichiometric (NaxFe0.125Ni0.125Mn0.75O2) and Mn-deficient (NaxFe0.125Ni0.125Mn0.68O2) NFNMO to identify and discuss the contribution of each element sublattice on charge compensation processes.  Although Mn deficiency is predicted to increase the cathode working voltage, we find the charge compensation being mostly exerted by the Ni and Fe sublattices.  Oxygen redox is unfold via the formation of superoxide species at low Na loads with a preferential breaking of more labile Ni-O bonds and binding to Fe atoms.  Our calcns. predict no release of mol. O2 upon desodiation, thus highlighting the key role of Fe dopant that provides a good TM-O bond strength, preventing oxygen loss while still enabling anionic redox reactions at high voltages with extra reversible capacity.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref77"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref77" class="refNumLink">77</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit77" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702998"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mo, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Computational Studies of Electrode Materials in Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Exploiting high-performance cathodes is still in need for sodium-ion batteries, which is crit. to promote their commercialization.  Layered sodium manganese oxide cathodes show low cost and natural abundance but suffer from poor cycling life and rate capacity.  Herein, electrochem. inert Ti4+ and active Ni2+ are used to replace some Mn ions in Na0.62MnO2, and neutron power diffraction results demonstrate a negligible change in the sizes of the metal layer and Na-ion layer in the structure.  Although Na0.62[Ni0.12Ti0.12Mn0.76]O2 and Na0.62MnO2 share the same Na content in pristine materials and theor. capacity, the improved performance of Na0.62[Ni0.12Ti0.12Mn0.76]O2 stems from the suppressed phase transitions and ordering process, alleviated Jahn-Teller distortion, and a high Na utilization of 73.8% compared with 62.2% for Na0.62MnO2. Na0.62[Ni0.12Ti0.12Mn0.76]O2 exhibits an av. working voltage of about 3.5 V, a great rate capability, and cycling stability of 76.8% capacity retention after 120 cycles in the voltage range of 2.5-4.5 V. A Mg content of 5% is sufficient to smooth the charge/discharge profiles without affecting the capacity, while further increasing the Mg content improves the cycling stability, but at the expense of a lower discharge capacity (∼150 mA h g-1 for Na0.67Mn0.8Mg0.2O2).  It was obsd. that the cooling process during synthesis, as well as Mg content, have an influence on the structure.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref80"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref80" class="refNumLink">80</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit80" data-doi="10.1002/nano.202000030"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Manganese-based Layered Oxide Cathodes for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Sel.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">2</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">200</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">225</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Engineering of Porous P2-Na<sub>2/3</sub>Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>2/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Nanofibers Assembled by Nanoparticles Enables Superior Sodium-Ion Storage Cathodes</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>30</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">6</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">1907837</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201907837</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical Engineering of Porous P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 Nanofibers Assembled by Nanoparticles Enables Superior Sodium-Ion Storage Cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Shen, Qiuyu; Zhao, Xudong; Zhang, Jian; Liu, Xiaobin; Wang, Tianshi; Zhang, Ning; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Jun; Fan, Li-Zhen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1907837</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered transition metal oxides (TMOs) are appealing cathode candidates for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) by virtue of their facile 2D Na+ diffusion paths and high theor. capacities but suffer from poor cycling stability.  Herein, taking P2-type Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 as an example, it is demonstrated that the hierarchical engineering of porous nanofibers assembled by nanoparticles can effectively boost the reaction kinetics and stabilize the structure.  The P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 nanofibers exhibit exceptional rate capability (166.7 mA h g-1 at 0.1 C with 73.4 mA h g-1 at 20 C) and significantly improved cycle life (≈81% capacity retention after 500 cycles) as cathode materials for SIBs.  The highly reversible structure evolution and Ni/Mn valence change during sodium insertion/extn. are verified by in operando X-ray diffraction and ex situ XPS, resp.  The facilitated electrode process kinetics are demonstrated by an addnl. study using the electrochem. measurements and d. functional theory computations.  More impressively, the prototype Na-ion full battery built with a Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 nanofibers cathode and hard carbon anode delivers a promising energy d. of 212.5 Wh kg-1.  The concept of designing a fibrous framework composed of small nanograins offers a new and generally applicable strategy for enhancing the Na-storage performance of layered TMO cathode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA06360K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Singh, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">López Del Amo, J. M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Galceran, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pérez-Villar, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rojo, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structural Evolution during Sodium Deintercalation/Intercalation in Na<sub>2/3</sub>[Fe<sub>1/2</sub>Mn<sub>1/2</sub>]O<sub>2</sub></span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">13</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">6954</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">6961</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C4TA06360K</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structural evolution during sodium deintercalation/intercalation in Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Singh, Gurpreet; Lopez del Amo, Juan Miguel; Galceran, Montserrat; Perez-Villar, Sofia; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6954-6961</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Among the various possible earth abundant electrode materials, P2-Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2 is one of the most promising cathode materials for sodium ion batteries.  Most transition metal oxide materials undergo various structural transitions during the sodiation/desodiation process and it is crucial to understand such transitions for further development of these materials.  In the present research, in situ XRD, in situ Raman spectroscopy and ex situ solid-state NMR were used as tools to understand such transitions for the specific case of P2-Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2.  Both in situ Raman spectroscopy and x-ray diffraction measurements, together with ex situ solid-state NMR studies revealed that the synthesized P2-Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2 hexagonal crystal structure undergoes P2-OP4 reversible phase transitions at the end of the charge process and at the end of the discharge process a biphasic mechanism follows.  Also, ex-situ solid state NMR measurements revealed the fast diffusion of Na+ ions in the 2-dimensional layers of P2-Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2, which led to an av. 23Na NMR signal that reflects very accurately the av. oxidn. state of the metal centers. P2-type manganese-based layered oxides have received special attention by virtue of their high theor. capacity, low cost, and environmental friendliness.  However, water sensitivity and limited cycling stability hinder their application, esp. since the underlying mechanisms for the above two issues are still unclear.  In this work, copper substitution is used to suppress the Jahn-Teller effect of Mn3+ and affect the corresponding lattice structure.  The water sensitivity and charge compensation mechanism were carefully investigated.  Results demonstrate that water sensitivity of the electrode is related to the order of Na+/vacancy in the Na interlayers since water mols. are more easily inserted into the charged state electrodes, but the tendency for the water uptake does not increase with Na+ extn.  Furthermore, Mn2+ forms on the surface of electrodes in the initial discharge process, and the redox reaction in the bulk is predominantly between Mn3+ and Mn4+.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na layered P2-stacking Na0.67MnO2 materials showed great promise for Na-ion batteries.  However, the undesired Jahn-Teller effect of the Mn4+/Mn3+ redox couple and multiple biphasic structural transitions during charge/discharge of the materials lead to anisotropic structure expansion and rapid capacity decay.  Herein, by introducing abundant Al into the transition-metal layers to decrease the no. of Mn3+, the authors obtain the low cost pure P2-type Na0.67AlxMn1-xO2 (x = 0.05, 0.1 and 0.2) materials with high structural stability and promising performance.  The Al-doping effect on the long/short range structural evolutions and electrochem. performances is further studied by combining in situ synchrotron XRD and solid-state NMR techniques.  The authors' results reveal that Al-doping alleviates the phase transformations thus giving rise to better cycling life, and leads to a larger spacing of Na+ layer thus producing a remarkable rate capability of 96 mAh g-1 at 1200 mA g-1.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.2c12894"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Study of Synergistic Effects of Cu and Fe on P2-Type Na<sub>0.67</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> for High Performance Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-type Na0.67MnO2 with a stable structure and an open framework can provide numerous channels for fast Na+ de/intercalation, for which it is considered to be advantageous in application of the cathode material for Na-ion batteries.  However, the complex phase transition occurring during cycling and the lattice distortion triggered by the Jahn-Teller effect severely restrict its development.  Herein, the modified Na0.67MnO2 with Cu or Fe single-element doping as well as Cu and Fe double-element doping was synthesized by the sol-gel method, and the effects of doping on the crystal structure and electrochem. performances of Na0.67MnO2 were studied.  It was demonstrated that the phase of the material did not change after the introduction of Cu and Fe elements, and the cycling stability and rate performance were greatly improved by Cu and Fe double-doping owing to their synergistic effect.  The Na0.67Mn0.92Fe0.04Cu0.04O2 (NMFCO) cathode delivers discharge specific capacities of 110.5 mA h g-1 at 5 C and 91.8 mA h g-1 at 10 C and exhibits the high-capacity retention of 94.35% at 1 C and 90.68% at 5 C after 100 cycles.  Overall, this study offers a guiding direction for accelerating the modification of P2-type Na0.67MnO2 as a cathode active material for high performance Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201805381"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.
